An excellent work-lunch-time game, or start-of-a-games-night game.

RATING: 6
Hmm. First, this game only plays reasonably well with 4 or more people. Second, it plays at times poorly due to odd card draws - like several traps in a row for several phases of the game. Third, I still kinda like it. But only in the right mood or setting. Lots of players. Pure filler. Pass the time. There is nearly zero strategy - but bluffing is really fun if the cards come out right. So in general, luck of the draw literally makes this game shine or stink for everyone. I'd say 1 out of 2 times it plays well.

RATING: 8.2
Very good game, and the archetypal "Gateway" game. Butchering someone elses quip, its like the game was hewn from a mine as one perfect flawless gaming nugget.
Although it's tiring after a few plays, where the laws of averages catch up with you, The game executes the "push-your-luck" mechanic perfectly, without artificial supports and with a great theme. Better than Can't Stop, Cosmic Wimpout et al by a long way. The only downside is the game is quite expensive for the weight.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Ican gold is a game whereby players dares other players to continue venturing into a cave to find treasures before they met the dangers in the cave.  Once players back out, they are allowed to keep whatever treasures they have found so far but not allowed to go back into the cave to look for more treasures in that round.

When players met any dangers, they lose all their treasures and went back to the camping area with no treasures.

Good points: The game has simple rules and can be explained in minutes.  The game can really be fun when it is played by many.

Bad points:  It is a pity to bend the cards as instructed in the game rules.  The game must be played by a rowdy group of players or it may not bring out the flavour of the game, to dare each other to venture further and get more treasures.

RATING: 6.5
The only reason that Incan Gold is getting a 6.5 from me is because I really like it with 6+ players. And I mean, I REALLY like it. Any less than that and it becomes sort of "meh". The gambling, push your luck, aspect of this game is something that gamers and non-gamers can latch on to. This game isn't meant to be serious. Part of the fun of this game can be pushing your luck in order to get farther into the temple than one of your friends.

This has been a big hit among my game group and among my family and that is huge. I love it when a game appeals to a wide audience and this certainly hits that spot.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Great for big numbers of player. Best games with groups of 8-9 to relax between harder games.
On the same level as MOW for that.

The base : when finding treasure, you always split up exactly between explorers, and any leftover is left in the room to pick on the way back. 
When finding perils, the first of each is harmless, but the second has all explorer left running back dropping all their treasure.

Very simple choice, just go on or go back.
Going on can mean more treasure, especially after other players go back the share goes up BUT you can also lose everything.
Going back mean keeping what you have already found, as well as picking up leftover gems on the way back, which can make a substantial bonus, especially if you go back alone.

Also good for non player/family
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5.5
I played this game with some of the kids at my work tonight and, as expected, it was a hit.  There is actually quite a lot going for this game as a math learning tool for young kids, mainly with division and probability.  I wavered about getting the Diamant version for a while, but decided on this version.  I think the artwork is nicer, especially the artifact cards, the gems are lackluster compared to Diamant, but it serves its purpose as an aesthetically pleasing, simple yet solid risk taking game.  

Update: one of my 5 year old son's favorite games.

RATING: 9
Good with 3 or more, to me really starts to shine with 5-8 players as it rewards pushing your luck more.  A very fun light game to play, where the conversation created during the playing is a big part of the fun.  A game which can be played and enjoyed by people of all ages.  I have played this with children aged 5-8 and find that they compete very well as they tend to be more risk adverse than some adults.  A good game to introduce non-gamers to.

When playing with my niece she is responsible for calculating how many rubies everyone gets, and what the remainder is, I mean what is left over and goes on the cards.  A pretty sneaky way to teach math.  Hope she doesn't figure it out!

I like the artifacts from the Inca Gold edition, but I like the components from the Diamant version better.  If I had to choose between the two it would be Diamant.  Holding the meeple in your hand is a lot cleaner and less confusing than having to choose correctly between 2 cards.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Successor to Diamant.  I like the components better in Diamant; the ore cart and the meeples.  To me holding the meeple in the hand is less confusing than trying to pick correctly which of the two cards you're supposed to use each turn.

On the other hand the inclusion of the artifact cards is a nice addition, and they do add another dimension to the game.  

I always play this game too aggressively.

RATING: 8
This is one of my favorite games for a large group.  Essentially this is a "push your luck" gambling game.  

Players take on the role of explorers looking for treasure in an abandoned Incan temple.  At every step the players have the option of taking what they found and leaving the temple to bank safely in their tents.  The less people exploring the temple the more lucrative the expedition...but the greater the danger to lose it all.

It plays fast (frequently in about 30 minutes) and leaves everyone involved...even if it's just to root and cheer for the remainders of an expedition to meet with disaster.

RATING: 8
[i]Posted: 1/11/08, Rated: 8[/i]

I was first introduced to [i]Diamant[/i] on [url=http://www.brettspielwelt.de/?nation=en]BrettspielWelt[/url].  It felt like a big randomfest (yes, I just made up a new word, I hope you'll forgive my precocious nature), and I didn't care for it.  Part of my reaction was due to my not fully understanding the rules, even though they aren't difficult.  The good news was that it never lasted very long.  Sometimes I even won, although I didn't know how I managed to do so.

Still...the game stuck with me.  And when my sons displayed a tenacious appetite for "press your luck" games, I remembered it.  Suddenly the Indiana Jones-esque (precocious) theme wasn't corny, it was cool.  Browsing the gallery showed inviting, fun images instead of the sterile, computer-rendered ones from BSW.  I decided it might be a game worth owning after all.

It turns out that [i]Diamant[/i] is a real gem when played face-to-face.  It is an extremely easy game to teach, and provides an enjoyable, social experience.  My family immediately took to it, and we've introduced it to other families with universal success.  It is a perfect, light "filler" game, that has the added benefit of being playable by up to eight people.  Despite my initial misgivings, [i]Diamant[/i] is a diamond in the rough.

RATING: 8
Incan Gold is simple, easy fun. It's a "press your luck" game that seems to solve a lot of negative issues present in other similar games. The cards apply equally to everyone, so you'll always feel like you have control over whether you win or lose. It's also very interactive, since you're constantly trying to guess what everyone else is going to do. And the door is open for different sorts of strategies: for example, instead of trying to stay in the temple as long as possible, it is perfectly viable to get out early and take all the jewels yet placed on the cards.

Unfortunately, the rulebook is quite vague (especially for the artifact rules), so make sure you check the forums for clarification.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A very nice press-your-luck game that seems to captivate everyone.  The amount of howls and moans as a second hazard strikes a player is hilarious.  My family really enjoys this type of game, and the way that this one involves all players at the same time is awesome.  It's also really nice that, with enough guts and luck, players can come back from any deficit.

The one issue is that you really should play with a large group (6 to 8 players is ideal.)  With less players, one good round will often determine who wins.  You also need to have everyone within easy reach of the stones.  If one player has to pass out all the stones to all the players they will get sick of the game really quickly.  But the game works really well with players of almost any age.

RATING: 7.5
Also printed as "Incan Gold", this is a classic push your luck game where the only decision you need to make is whether t keep going further in the cave to discover more treasure, or to run away and garb treasures already discovered. The catch is that if you and another player leave at the same time, you must split the treasure available, and if you stay in too long, you may succumb to the dangers within. 

Simple fun, and only about 30 min, this game works with gamers and non-gamers alike, and can play a crowd to boot!

RATING: 7
Fun light filler game for the entire family.
before you say its pure luck (and luck play a big part) keep in mind that its actually a probability game.
What is the expected value of going further, vs. cashing out now?
Ex: I have X treasures, and drawing 1 card gives me a D percentage of disaster vs. an expected Treasure value.
It also helps if you try and be aware of the other players holdings as it gives you an idea of whether you need to press your luck.

(PS - dont forget to remove a disaster card if it triggers the end of the round)

RATING: 7
Fun filler type game. I played this as "Incan Gold" but it was exactly the same game. 

Each person gets to decide to run or push into the temple before another card is revealed. This could be treasure of different value, an artifact or a trap. Think Indiana Jones here. The fun part is deciding to keep pushing your luck or run for safety with the treasure you have collected at that point. There's only 5 rounds and these only last a few minutes each. This is another game that you can pretty much just start playing. Explaining the rules only takes a minute or two.

This is a really nice, light, push-your-luck game that works very well with large groups (up to 8) and for non-gamers as well! I prefer this version of the game, rather than Incan Gold, for the bits. Incan Gold includes some additional "treasure" cards, but they don't make up for the lack of meeples and folded card "tent" instead of the very nifty cardboard crates to hold the diamonds.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I'm not sure if my family and I are all mutants, but this game kind of fell flat for us after the first few plays; it does not hit the table often now.  I agree that it is good for teaching some basic math skills, such as simple division (since you have to divide jewels equally between players still in the cave).  And how many games teach kids division in a  fun way?  So that is a good thing about  the game to be sure.  However, as I said I have worries about replayability.  There's a certain sameness to each game.  Go in the cave.  Do I get out now?  No, maybe now?  Ok, now.  Then go in the cave again.  Do I go out now?  No, maybe now.  Ok, now.  Then go in the cave again.  And so on.  As far as push-your-luck games go, I prefer Cloud 9.  The theme is not as exciting, but there's more player interaction (since there is a bluffing element to that game).  Cloud 9 doesn't teach division though!  So if you are looking for a fun game with a math element, I could still recommend Incan Gold.  Otherwise I think there are better games.  Still, remember my family may be mutants and take that into consideration.

Plays:  around 10, each for 4 players (2 adults, 2 kids aged 7 and 5)

RATING: 8.5
Diamant (1st edition): 8.5 Wonderful game - lots of fun and immensely replayable.  It's light and fast and the decison whether to flee or stay is usually finely balanced.  The lovely wee jewels, chunky explorer meeples and handy treasure cartons of the 'Diamant' edition make it the one to get.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Incan Gold: 7.5 Pretty much the same game as Diamant, but docked a full point for inferior presentation (no lovely jewels) and annoying component changes (why get rid of the meeples - which were such an elegant solution). While I like the maguffins in this version, others don't. If you have a choice, get Diamant instead. If you can't then this remains a good game.

RATING: 7
Definitely a fluffy filler with a lot of randomness and not super thinky, but I like this one. A combination of push your luck and prisoner's dilemma in equal proportions, comically easy to explain and over in time to get to something meatier (which is to say, just about anything.) Before the mania for "microgames" swept the boardgame community, there were solid, modest little timekiller games like this one, that set out to do what they intended.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
What filler should aspire to. Very fast, very easy to teach, variable enough to make you want to sit down to it anytime you have 15 minutes left over. Each turn a new card is flipped over with gems or traps / obstacles on it. If it has gems, then each player present gets a cut, with the remainder being left on the card. If it's an obstacle nothing happens until a duplicate is drawn, once the second is drawn then the expedition is over and the players who are still in the cave lose all of the gems they have collected. An additional incentive to leave is that the players who flee collect any left-over gems on the cards that have already been discovered, and in the case of relics, if they flee alone, then they get to pick up any relic cards that have been flipped as well that are worth 5-10 points depending on how many have already been collected.

The  "should I run" mechanic remind me both of Ra (for the push your luck aspect) and a myriad of bluffing games (because cutting and running is most lucrative when no one else is doing it at the same time). This is highlighted further in the later editions that add the 5 relics to the game.

One warning: this rating is reflective only of high scale games (5+), because of the way the game works it isn't nearly as good with less, so I would only get this if you actually have a group large enough to handle it. The beauty is that more players does almost nothing to increase the game length, but adds multiple areas in which players can bump heads when they go to leave the expedition.

Many printings exist, but the originals from Schmidt do not have the relics, which is a shame, as I like the original art best. From the perspective of art and functionality to value I think the current Iello edition is probably the best, as I like the square cards for this one and it also has nice little cardboard chests to hide your loot in.

RATING: 7
So fun! I love the push your luck factor. 

I had a neighbor we played this with who kept going and kept going long after everyone else had fled to their tents. (this is a fun game condition that occurs every few plays of the game) He was able to flip cards at will and keep all the loot for himself. After 20 or more cards flipped we were all on the edge of our seats begging him to take in his epic haul but he kept trolling us with more and more flipping. Ultimately, he took in something like 60 or 70 points in one round when he chose to leave the temple with his loot. Of course, we always like to flip the next card to see what might have been...the very next card ended up being the one that would have cost him everything! It's this kind of stuff that makes Incan Gold so fun to play. To me it's a little like Yahtzee in that I can be really excited for other people when they rock it without getting too competitive or upset that I'm losing horribly.

RATING: 7.5
The gameplay is basically a really fancy version of the timeless classic game "which hand?"  You really only have two choices at any given time; stay or go.  That's it.  

So how is this so ridiculously fun?  It just is.  Rather than condemning it for it's simplicity, I think it's about time we start giving "which hand?" the recognition it deserves. :laugh:

Must say though, that the little 2/3 size cards are a pain to shuffle, and it's hard to sneak your little meeple into your hand when playing on a glass table.

RATING: 6
Diamant version.

The ultimate large group non-gamer filler game.

Kids burned out on this one pretty quickly.  Its a good game for a large group though.  I can get my kids to play this one once in a while.

Very good for drawing non-gamers into games though.  Bought some extra red "gems" at Hobby Lobby to help handle large groups which is usually how I play this game.  Otherwise, there is a lot of down-time as people exchange their gems.

If you play with kids, make it a point to have them administer the gems.  This is a GREAT game to teach division/remainders.  There are 5 travelers, and 17 gems were found.  Each traveler is awarded 3 gems and 2 are left on the path.

RATING: 5
A simple push-your-luck game that has absolutely beautiful bits.  The more people playing, the better the game will be.  

We've added a rule where everyone has to reveal whether they are going forward or going back to camp at the same time by using a "one two shoot" method--where on "shoot" everyone has to either point forward (to show they are going forward) or keep a closed fist (to show they are going back).  This ends up being one of the more fun elements of the game.

I paid a bunch of money for the German version with the board (base camp).  I could have purchased Incan Gold instead, but the board art, the explorer meeples, the pretty jewels... all these things make the game that much more enjoyable.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.2
Players enter 5 caves (rounds) in search of rubies and diamonds (each diamond = 5 rubies), but they have to make sure to get out before the cave collapses. The latter happens if the second card of 1 of 5 types of dangers is drawn. Each turn a card is drawn, showing a number of rubies, a danger or a relic (worth 1 or 2 diamonds). The number of rubies is split amongst all the adventurers equally. The rubies that cannot be equally split, remain on the card until 1 or more players decide to return. If only 1 returns he can take all the rubies that were left behind, as well as the relics, if more than 1 player returns at the same time, they have to share the rubies equally and get no relics...After each card the players have to show contemporaneously whether or not they want to return from the cave, by taking a playing piece in their hand under the table and revealing what they are holding in their hand. Players who fail to return before the cave collapses loose everything they gathered in the tunnel.

RATING: 8.5
Ok, this game is a great to play with families with a wide age range of kids.  There is really only one decision to make each round- stay in the temple or leave, and then the round plays itself out.  This makes it accessible to my little one and my teen.  A surprising amount of tension builds on those decisions and it's fun to experience this together.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This game is extremely simplistic, which is both an asset and a flaw. The game boils down to a simple decision: do I stay or do I go? This makes the game very easy to teach (in about 5 minutes or less) and plays well with people who enjoy gambling or are risk takers. The game is also mindless enough that it can be played as a side activity to something else, such as watching tv.

The advantage to staying in the temple is the potential for more gems but at the risk of losing it all to a matching hazard. The advantage of going is to pick up all leftover gems on the way out and to secure any gems collected that round at the risk of losing out on anything else that comes after you've left. Leaving also has an added wrinkle of having to split all gems (and leave behind artifacts) if multiple players leave at once, meaning you don't always want to leave when everyone else does.

However, the choice to stay or go is rarely interesting. Most of the times my players couldn't even bother to use the cards, they'd just blurt out if they were staying or going (which quite frankly gives a huge advantage to the last player to call out). The only time the decisions are fun are when a player is on a long streak of cards and keeps pushing the deck. Naturally, these moments are the central mechanic of the game, yet they are so far and few between that the slog to get to them often overwhelms them. Speaking of slogs, the game is about 2 rounds too long. It doesn't seem necessary to go beyond 3 rounds, as it just drags the game out longer.

The artwork is a bit dry. The theme comes through enough, but it just seems very generic. For instance, you're supposed to show players which artifact is being added at the beginning of a new round in a sort of ooh-and-ah moment... and yet there's no discernible reason to do so. All the artifacts are the same for gameplay purposes and the artwork isn't noteworthy enough to mention every round. The only card I ever point out is the artifact that kind of looks like a toilet. There's also lots of debate on the stay and go cards whenever I teach the game. They look very similar to each other and do not contain any words on them to indicate which is which. This was likely to keep the game language independent, but EVERY SINGLE TIME I teach this game I have to remind new players which card is which multiple times. They'll often even try to argue with me, citing something in the artwork as to why the stay card should be the leave card. It seems so trivial a thing to label the cards and yet they just didn't bother.

Which is generally how I feel about the game. I can't be bothered to sit through five rounds of making boring decisions. The theme is dry, the decisions are dull, and the game doesn't give enough of those how-far-can-I-go moments to justify my attention. Even as the light filler game it is, this just feels stale. I keep the game because my family enjoys it and it's simple to teach on holidays, but I generally don't enjoy my time with it.

PS: I always find myself humming the lyrics to The Clash's song while playing.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Players explore a cave stuffed with gems, attempting to be the player with the most at the end of five rounds.  Each turn a cave card is flipped up from a deck of 30 cards.  It's either a numbered gem card, or a disaster card.  Gem cards split the number of gems between the players, with remainder staying on the card.  Disaster cards do nothing until the second disaster of that type appears.  Each round players have the option of staying in the cave and risking this rounds collection, or bugging out and "banking" their gems (plus cave remainders).   Repeat over five rounds.  The game screams "Cloud 9", which isn't a surprise given the designers, but is easier to pick up and play than that venerable classic, and works better with more people.  Lovely bits.

Did someone play their card to leave the temple?  Funny!  Did someone stay in for more treasure?  Funny!  Was someone able to overcome some odds and find some big treasure?  Awesome!  Did that same person foolishly stay in one turn too long?  Even better!  I'm not scoring this an 8 and claiming it's better than, or on par with, other great games (think Terra Mystica, Agricola, etc...); I'm scoring an 8 because I'll always enjoy this, will recommend it, and probably never turn down a game.  It's excellently fun for anyone.

RATING: 6.5
I actually read the rules for this while the group was busy finishing up another game and taught it immediately after.  It wasn't even my copy.

At any rate, Incan Gold is a simple press-your-luck game with some great components - the cards were all linen stock and the gems were all nicely made.  On your turn, you simply decide whether you want to see the next card in the deck or take whatever spoils you've gathered so far back home and leave the other players to whatever dangers lie ahead.  That's pretty much the gist of the game.

It works like this - On a draw of a treasure card, everyone splits it down the middle and the remainder is left on the path.  If a danger card is drawn, no problem.  If a second danger card of the same type is drawn, everyone still in the temple goes home empty handed.  If an artifact is drawn, nobody gets to take it unless they are the [i]only[/i] one to choose to go home.  If you decide to go home early, you and whoever else not only gets to keep what you've already picked up, but you also get to split whatever was left on the path (minus artifacts).

That's it.  It's that simple.  It's a lot of fun with the right group, and it's really deadly for anyone who has a gambling problem haha.

RATING: 6
Incan Gold is a push-your-luck game that accommodates a large number of players. It's also really easy rules-wise and plays relatively quickly. During a turn, each player simultaneously chooses whether continue exploring (which flips one card, which will have wealth or a hazard) or pass (bank dived wealth and divide leftover wealth among leaving players). If doubles of a particular hazard happens, players who have been exploring, lose the opportunity to bank their wealth. Incan Gold is more recent iteration of the game Diamant. While I feel Diamant has nicer components, Incan Gold has some additional gameplay mechanisms that make the game more fun. Iello will be doing a new edition of Diamant in 2016 which will included Incan Gold's enhancements but Diamant's superior components. So, it should be the best of both worlds.

RATING: 6
A purely press-your-luck game that actually lets you press your luck twice. The first and most obvious press is choosing whether or not to continue exploring (pressing against the deck), but the second is choosing when to leave the temple (pressing against your opponents). Incan Gold glimmers most at higher player counts when the social deduction element associated with that second press is at its most excruciating. The rapid play time, and scalability make this a worthy press-your-luck addition.

RATING: 5
[1 play] I can’t really see why this has a separate entry from Diamant, but I guess that’s a controversy for another thread.   I had played Diamant once or twice some time back when I tried Incan Gold.  The play is much the same, to the best of my recollection, but in terms of production, Diamant has the edge in several ways.  

The most annoying thing about Incan Gold is the stay or go cards.  In Diamant you do this with a little piece that you do or don’t have in your hand; everyone puts their hands out, and then you show.  With Incan Gold it’s two different cards, and the super-annoying thing about them is how similar looking they are.  Both have a picture of a guy in a cave with a torch.  The picture isn’t the same, and when you look closely you see that on the "Go" card, you can see the tent in the background through the mouth of the cave, the torch has burned lower, and the guy is now carrying a sack of treasure.  Nice thematic details, but what you need here is two cards that really obviously differentiate themselves at a glance, both to avoid making mistakes on your own play (which did happen in our game at least once) and so that when cards are revealed, you can immediately see what everyone did.  I call this a definite design fail.

Incan Gold did offer one unique and somewhat hair-raising experience.  My friend’s copy was new, and we had to set up the tents ourselves, by bending the cards.  It gives me the creeps just to write that, but yes, bending the cards.  I deliberately took a playing card and bent it in half and creased the hell out of it.  And I have to say, it felt perverse and wrong.

RATING: 6
"Should I stay or should I go!?" - The Clash... Literally, that is the game.

This game is beautifully simplistic and fantastic to play with kids because it is so intuitive and effectively an older player can run it like a casino game.  For an adult it's ok but a little lacking, my personal preference leads towards Celestia but with kids, this one wins hands-down, every time.

Comparatively to Celestia this one works on known odds so it is in that sense a little more mathematically strategic in the same way a game like Blackjack is where as Celestia is more social and a bit of luck.

This game will be a clear hit or miss depending on what you are after.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Reasonably fun filler that will take up to 8. 

It's played over five rounds each consisting of a variable amount of turns.

Each turn a card is turned over and it will either have a number on it or one of several hazards. If it has a number, gems are shared out amongst the players with the remainder going on the card. Once two hazzards of the same type appear in a system, that round is over and you lose any gems that aren't safely put away. 

Each player then simultaneously decides whether to take the gems and put them away safely for another round. Last player in takes the gems from the cave.

RATING: 8
This is quite a fun game!  It rewards taking risks, but also sensible timing of when to bail and take extra points along the way.  There's a good amount of suspense when waiting for the next card.  When hazards cause disasterous results, one of the bad cards is removed to increase the chances for the players on the next round.

Simple, elegant, and PURE FUN!  Probably my favorite "push-your-luck" type game.  Grade: B

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Only played it with 3 so far. As such, I would rate it a 6. But I can see it become more (party) fun with more players, therefor a 7.

It's a nice & quick Can't Stop like game, with a little added math, some bluffing & a bit of interaction. But apart from that, there's still not much more than plain luck in here. You could f.i. draw a snake, then a small treasure, everyone decides to continue exploring and if then by accident the next card would already be the next snake, the round is over. Sessions that don't have such early buggers can be huge fun, but with at least two rounds finishing this quickly, it takes away quite a bit of the fun. I would have given it a higher score, if somehow the danger could be anticipated a bit more.

A small variant could be to take out 10 cards before each round and divide them over piles of 2, 3 & 5 cards next to the temple. A player could pay this amount of gems to take a look at the cards that won't show up in the path to explore. More and probably even better variants can be thought of, but still I can't see how you could avoid rounds to possibly end after just a couple of cards. Though maybe it could help to state that a round would only finish after the 2nd PAIR of danger cards being revealed ?

20 min, 3-8, cardgame
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Minimalistic game of chicken for larger groups.

Players are collectively exploring a cave in search of treasure by flipping cards that either have a pile of gems or a hazard on it. Any gems found are divided equally by the players, leaving any remaining gems on the card. Hazard cards come in a few varieties (for example snakes), with three cards of each variety. The hazard cards don't give any pay-out, and whenever a second card of any type is revealed, all players still exploring the cave lose all gems they carry. 

Before revealing the next card to explore, all players choose simultaneously if they want to continue on or go back to the camp with whatever gems they have found so far. Players returning to the camp are allowed to pick up any gems that were previously left on the cards, but if more than one player are returning at the same time, they must again share the loot equally.

After all players have either returned to the camp safely or succumbed to one of the dangers in the cave, the cards are reshuffled and the players have a go at exploring the next cave. At the conclusion of the fifth cave exploration, the player with the most collected gems wins.

The choices you make during the game are not very deep nor particularly interesting, and the game is very reliant on there being a fitting social atmosphere for it to be much fun. You can do some card counting to figure out your chances, and there is a timing problem of when to bolt for the exit. But in practice the game relies much more on the group dynamics of the players. This makes the game very dependant on the group playing it, and it falls flat if nobody is in the right mood. Also, the number of players greatly changes the dynamics of the game and it seems to play much better with larger groups. 

But still, the game doesn't do anything particularly wrong either. As long as it's seen as a 15 minute push-you-luck party game for groups of minimum five players I think it works well.

[JAN 09] [Rating: 5]

Or maybe I just enjoy hoarding plastic gems.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Tütütütü-tütütü-tütütütü-tü-tü-tü-tü
Egyik kedvenc partijátékomról nem nehéz dicsérő szavakat írnom. 3-8 játékos (2 játékos variáns is van) kincskereső kalandorokat, Indiana Jones-okat testesítenek meg, akik Közép-Amerika egyik ősi templomának 5 szintjét végigkutatva próbálják a legtöbb értéket magukénak tudni.
Mindenki egy csapatban indul neki az egyes szinteknek (5 fordulóból áll egy játék), majd lépésről lépésre fedik fel a húzópakli lapjait, amelyek a folyosón található kincseket/ereklyéket vagy veszedelmeket ábrázolják.
Amint kincset találnak, egyenlően osztozkodnak (a többlet kincs rákerül a felhúzott kártyára) és mindenki eldönti, hogy tovább marad bent a templomban vagy az eddig megszerzett „loot”-al együtt elhagyja azt (plusz távozáskor felveheti a kártyán vagy kártyákon rajtamaradt többlet kincset is. Itt is egyenlően kell osztozkodni, ha többen távoznak egyszerre; tehát előfordulhat, hogy senki nem kap a kártyákról semmit, ha többen is távoznak egyszerre, mint amennyi felé osztható lenne a rajtamaradt kincs).
A döntését kártyalap (fáklya vagy tábor kártya = bent marad vagy távozik) felmutatásával jelzi, amelyet mindenki egyszerre hajt végre.
A távozók a megszerzett kincseket eltehetik kis sátraikba a többiek számláló szemétől elrejtve, míg a bent maradó játékosok új lapot húznak fel.
Hogy ne legyen egyszerű az élet, a húzópakliban a játék kezdetén 5 típusú veszedelemből (kőomlás, zombi pap, pókok, tűzdémon, kígyó) 3-3 lap kerül bele.
Amikor lapot húz a csapat és egy veszedelem kerül felfedésre az alábbi történhet. 1. Amennyiben még nem került ugyanilyen típusú veszedelem felhúzásra, semmi nem történik. 2. Amennyiben már került ilyen típusú veszedelem felhúzásra, a bent maradt kalandorok kincseiket hátrahagyva kimenekülnek a Templomból (nem kapnak semmit ebben a fordulóban). Valamint ez a veszedelem kártya kikerül a játékból (csökkentve a későbbi fordulókban megjelenő veszedelmeket).
Plusz minden fordulóban a pakliba kerül 1-1 értékes ereklye is (így az utolsó fordulóban akár 4-5 ereklye is lehet a pakliban). Viszont az ereklyét mindig csak egyetlen egy távozó kincsvadász viheti ki, ha többen távoznak egyszerre, az a helyén marad és a későbbiekben távozó kalandorok egyike szerezheti meg.
Tehát a tipikus „elég bátor vagy, hogy húzz még egy lapot” játékmenetet a fenti „fűszerek” ízesítik kellemes eledellé. Kockáztatsz vagy nem. Néha muszáj, de egy-egy megfontoltabb lépéssel is megnyerhető a parti.
Picit érthetetlen, hogy hazai piacon miért nem lehet beszerezni ezt a játékot. Egyszerű szabályok, gyors játékmenet, izgalom és vidámság. Szívesen ajánlom mindenkinek.

RATING: 6
Diamant is a quick and simple push-your-luck game with beautiful production value. The decisions every turn happen incredibly fast, either you're in or your out. Because of ease-of-play, it's not difficult to teach to non-gamers. Furthermore, this isn't a game in which all players are playing in parallel, there's built in incentive to make otherwise counter-intuitive moves to jump out of the competition to grab stray gems left behind on the path. This gives the game a bit of meat for more hardened gamers. Overall, a great fast-paced excercise in risk-management that does not overstay its welcome.

RATING: 7.75
Played with a 5 year old, and he won. However, adults won't be bored while playing. This is the ultimate gateway game. It takes 4 minutes to explain. Replay value is medium. The game does require removing the enter/exit cards, and using the alternate bravery beads as suggested on this site. Additionally, the 1-5 cards add nothing to the game, but to confuse new players, so it's best to remove them, and use the unplaced idols as a way to see what round you're on.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
What allows you to openly enjoy the suffering of your fellow players on their loss of treasure? What has very simple rules, fast play, that accommodates up to 8 players? Diamant! or Inca Gold! or whatever incarnation it currently is. The push-your-luck factor is way up there, and as a party game, this simply rocks. Admittedly, the diamond and ruby plastic gems are a beauty to behold, versus the current opaque stuff. The bid mechanic where you palm or don't palm your adventurer is quicker than the current card selection method. The box seems bigger than it should be though, and the game (in either version) seems way overpriced for what you get. Also, since it is soooo simple, about one play is all that most can stand in an evening.

Update (10/10/09): Well, the game is a little bit more sophisticated than I gave it credit for, since we were playing it slightly wrong--the leftover gems are not added to subsequent treasure finds and divided up; they are only picked up by explorers who are leaving! This significantly alters the dynamics of play, as now there is an incentive to leave earlier than usual. The crafty player who knows when to leave and take what he/she can get will usually win.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Played the 2009 Gryphon version after playing Diamant previously. In general, the artwork/graphics is superior to the earlier edition. There are more gems, and more colors, but not as enticing as the rubies and diamonds of Diamant. The cards are linen-finished and slick. The tents are more functional, although flimsier than the thick-cardboard chests of Diamant. Gone is the wooden expedition meeple, replaced by a pair of "in or out" cards, which is functionally equivalent, but the tactile feel of the meeple in hand is somewhat missed. The artifacts give an additional layer of strategy to leave earlier, which elevates what is a good party game filler to a very good filler that plays up to 8 players, all in 20-30 minutes.

Update (01/11/13) 12 plays: Just because it can handle up to 8 players doesn't mean you should necessarily play this. Tried it out on seven board gaming neophytes, and it was a mixed bag. The problem is that the game's sweet spot is probably around five players, not eight. This is because most of the time, the 8 players are not getting anything, and at most two gems if a '17' card pops up. Everyone will stay, since nothing exciting is happening, and then it is all disappointment when a second catastrophe strikes. So, the overall first-impressions are ho-hum. It does tend to get better, as the tension mounts. Some people got excited, while others were being put to sleep. It was slightly better with the second play, as some were frantic to try bettering their scores (of zero, or a few gems)! Can't satisfy everyone all the time.

Mindless.  It isn't a game, it is a psychology experiment.  I had more fun removing an ingrown hair.  Totally a runaway leader game. Incan Gold
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Ideal Players: 4-8

Description: Mine for precious jewels. The longer you mine the greater the reward, but the greater the risk of losing it all.

Pro: Great press-your-luck mechanic provides the ability to come back from behind. Fun prisoner's dilemma situation when deciding to cut out with your treasure. Simple enough to be easily accessible to casual gamers. Mechanics are very appropriate for the theme. Great components.

Con: Minimal complexity and strategy. Graphics could have more detail and variety.

RATING: 8
Great family game, great filler!  Also, as has been pointed out to me, would make the BEST drinking game.  A lot of laughter, a lot of suspense, with good production value, I really like this game a lot, and it is always popular, especially at the end of a game night.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Incan Gold is a solid luck-pushing game. It has a few issues such as rules that always seem to be a little confusing for new players (especially regarding what happens to treasures when players leave the temple), the potential for some players to wind up so far behind that can't leave the temple in the late rounds, and the unclear artwork on the decision cards (I've seen quite a few people play the wrong card accidentally).

In spite of its flaws, it can be an absolute riot. There can be real drama in how the game unfolds, everything from players waiting one card too long to flee to players who leave too early only to find out that the next several cards provided a plethora of treasures. That along with its short play length and ability to support a large number of players makes it a solid addition to one's game library.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

2014-08-25

Incan Gold was one of the first games I ever played, it can be fun with the right crowd, but nowadays I don’t have the slightest wish to play it. It is way too basic and simple for my current tastes. Still I recognize it can be a blast. Its main strengths are: 1. Very easy to teach. 2. It plays quickly and 3. It can accommodate a large number of players without significantly add to the game time.

I dislike that I had to bend the tent cards.

I’m sure I will play again, but this is not a game I will ever request.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Incan Gold is a simple, faced paced card game that's good in casual settings. Each player is an explorer looting an Incan temple. At the beginning of the turn, players simultaneously reveal whether they are going deeper into the temple or heading back to camp with their treasure. As the game goes on, players who have not returned to camp yet face greater odds of losing all of their treasure from the current round. So, Incan Gold is about pressing your luck and knowing when to quit. Sometimes, you'll score big for leaving at the right time. Sometimes, you'll score big for pushing onward after everyone else bails out. Nice artwork. Not as good as For Sale, No Thanks!, Liar's Dice, or Master of Rules, but passable. Better than Coloretto, at least. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Another great game by Gryphon Games. Explore an Incan tomb and get out while the getting is still good. A fun fast paced, and quick game, mostly based on luck and how much of a risk you want to take. The art and the game pieces are cool. And we always have fun playing it.

RATING: 5
In this push-your-luck game of tile flipping your only choice each turn is whether to stay or go, the prospective payout for each option depending on tiles flipped, the total number of players, and simultaneous decisions of other players. At least given attractive components and a slightly fatalistic approach I reckon this could be a decent entry-level game and game theory exercise. Some observations, which together may or may not be taken as flaws: 1) When a player is allowed to remain alone in an expedition, the flipping of tiles can be extremely swingy: a single tile can give them a significant portion of the points a safe strategy can yield for the entire game. 2) It is not very uncommon for an expedition to end before anyone has had a chance to earn a non-negligible amount of points, meaning many games will effectively have four or even three expeditions. This obviously matters a lot more if someone gets an early lead. 3) Once someone has a good lead, each other player has no choice but to adopt a risky strategy for the remainder of the game, or until they strike lucky themselves. (Of course, if scores are hidden and untracked, a player may unwittingly surrender any hope of winning.) 4) The more players adopt a risky strategy, the more all of their prospects are reduced. 5) Consequently, adopting an early safe strategy amounts to betting that no player will be risky and lucky, and conversely, adopting an early risky strategy amounts to betting that at least one risky player will be lucky. In either case, as soon as someone that is not you is both risky and lucky, you are almost certainly playing out a losing game. 6) Players should divide somewhat evenly into safe and risky in order for the game to be balanced overall. A lone risky player should have the highest chance to win, followed by a lone safe player.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
[size=12][b]Top 200 board games list[/b][/size]

[size=12][b]Why I like Diamant:[/b][/size]
+ I like pure push your luck games because they are excellent filler game. In terms of light games I vastly prefer push your luck games over deduction games.
+ The game is easy to teach
+ The game is short
+ There is high player involvement

[size=12][b]Why I dislike Diamant:[/b][/size]
- There are hardly any meaningful decisions to make as several aspects to the game are random. I only ignore this issue in regards to push your luck games because the focus of the game is luck.
- There could be better replayability. I think that this game could be integrated into another more complex game. 

[size=12][b]VERDICT:[/b] Keep & Sometimes willing to play this game[/size]

RATING: N/A
Incan Gold is a quick, fun and tense game in which you and other adventurers explore an old Incan temple in search of gold and treasure. In each of the five rounds, you secretly choose if you want to continue exploring the temple in search of more treasure or retreat to the safety of your camp with your share of the treasure that has been discovered so far.

RATING: 6
Excellent filler, although it wears out its welcome relatively quickly.  This is a pure push-your-luck game, and as such, there is little in the way of strategy.  The early goings of each round are rather unsuspenseful, but the tension rachets up quickly as more cards are laid down.  It seems that it's pretty easy to get busted in this game, which may encourage more conservative play than what would provide the most fun.  This is a game that can be played a max of twice in a night.  Any more than that and it gets a little old and tired.
UPDATE:  Played this with 8 for the first time.  The gameplay improves dramatically with that number.  The tension mounts quickly as much more treasure (I have Incan Gold) is left in the temples.  It becomes more tempting to leave earlier, but there is a lot of second-guessing.  The decision as to when to leave is not all about how much treasure is in front of you, but about how much treasure you can pick up on the way out.  I like the addition of the artifacts in Incan Gold.  It makes for some other interesting decisions, because only if you leave the temple alone can you take an artifact.  For 8 players, this is an "8" for me, especially because there aren't a lot of good games for 8 players.  I'll keep my rating at a "6," however, for groups of 6 and fewer.

RATING: 7
A simple press your luck filler game.  It is a game that anyone can quickly learn.  I would view it almost as a party game it is so light and easy to play.  You flip a card and if it has gems you divide amongst all player and leave remainders on the card.  You then decide to stay or go.  If two disasters of the same type come up, you lose everything you have gained.  If you run away, you get your gems and the remainder that is left. 

Simple and fun.  I think everyone should own this game.  It is a great filler.

RATING: 5.5
This game is a filler in the truest sense of the term. It combines the push-your-luck of Blackjack with a small amount of bluffing a la 5 card draw poker - as a filler this game is interesting in short bursts, but it won't satisfy as the main event. Of course, as a filler, it's worth picking up if you need something that 8 players can play in 20 minutes.

It does not over stay it's welcome either. There is plenty of replay-ability here. The components are serviceable, nothing fancy. It isn't flashy and could use a good makeover to bring it into the modern era of board/card gaming. But functionally everything works well and is simple to grasp, fun and quick. The push your luck element is good for some funny moments, and laughs.

RATING: 8
This game is an event and I love it.

Remember, once everyone has chosen their card, you do the drumming cadence in unison "shJAgita shJAgita shJAgita shJAgita shJUga shJUga JA!" (flip on final JA)

Dealer... as you reveal the next room, the Indiana Jones theme Opening Hook followed by...

Idol = Zelda Treasure Box Sound
Treasure = Second riff of Indy
Hazard = Falling note Wa-Wa
Second Hazard / Disaster = Price is Right Failure riff

No... I'm not kidding.  But then I've been told playing this game with me and my friends increases the fun significantly.

RATING: 7
An easy pick-up-and-go game — both that you grab-n-go but also you can just open it up and play even from the first outing. Simple, tile-laying, press-your-luck game without much else to it, but strangely satisfying. The components are excellent — the Indiana Jones meeples and actual treasure chests really make for a nice tactile experience. A game plays quickly, it’s easy to set up and put away, and it’s fun enough to play that it doesn’t really seem to matter who wins, because (usually) everybody gets some treasure. In the treasure box. And that’s neat.

RATING: 6.5
Played Incan Gold a couple times and found it fun.  Sometimes it's just pushing your luck, sometimes it's more about predicting your opponents' decisions.  Either way, there's not an awful lot of strategery involved, so the game moves quickly.  The excitement of the huge wins and sudden losses seems to make up for the over-dependence on luck; despite the fact that the game's playing you a bit more than you're playing it, you still have a lot of fun.  It's not one I'll want to play when I'm in a serious gaming mood, but it's a good warm-up or end-of-the-night game.

RATING: 7.5
Now this game was something else. Probably the best game I have ever had of Incan Gold. 

My son had a sleepover for his birthday (seems to be a modern invention that is becoming a kind of rites of passage for very young kids ... never had them in my day, it was just a natural occurrance when you got left behind at a party your parents had been too! ). Any way we had a group of about 8-10 8 year olds staying over for the night, the next morning my wife had to pop out for a while and left me alone with the horde ... I needed to think of something and think of it quick before Lord of the Flies type carnage descended on us all.

Out came Incan Gold my trusted friend ...

... and it has still never let me down. The game went down a treat with the kids screaming and shouting and that was just over the maths of calculating how many jewels to share out and what to leave on the path! The kids formed a band (with my middle daughter on saxophone) to play a musical accompaniment to the numerous copies of Mrs. Doyle who had sprung up encouraging everyone to go on. 



They even had an intermission from the game to work on the "Go On" song. It was hilarious watching them all sing along as we were choosing our cards to indicate go on further or run back to the tent. You could see in the eye's of one or two of them that they were panicking about the possibility of a second snake or spider turning up and grabbing them and this then turning to joy when, upon revealing the cards, everyone else had been swayed by the masses and ran headlong into the outstretched arms of a newly revealed second mummy whilst they returned to their tent triumphantly sweeping up all the jewels on the pathway back before them.

Just such a good game. I have had many requests from parents asking which game this was ... just fantastic fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Here are the things I like about Incan Gold.
- It can play up to 8 players.
- There's always someone to root for and someone to root against, and there's always someone rooting for or against you.
- The artifacts present a double-thinking aspect that's fun.
- Each round has slightly higher odds of scoring big than previous rounds.


Here are the things I don't like about Incan Gold:
- If a player banks a significant lead, they likely have already won the game.
- All those little gems have to get moved around each turn. Someone needs to play banker, basically.
- Often, a round ends before it hardly even gets interesting. A matching hazard card will come out and finish the round when everyone has 4 points.

Replaced by Deep Sea Adventure

RATING: 5
01/17/17 I played four games of 2P Incan Gold. My impression of Incan Gold after playing it was about the same as right after I heard its rules. Its a fair filler game, that *really* needs at least three players. So my initial outing tonight with only two lost some of its flavor, as expected. Therefore I rated it a "5" on BGG. That might go up 
if/when I play it with more people. But overall the "push your luck" mechanic is not one of my favorites. So I can't ever see myself rating it more than a 6. To me Incan Gold is almost a party type games. A type I try to avoid. 
- 01/31/17 I played two 5P games of Incan Gold. The game owner assured me it was much better with 3 to 8. The game was better with more. Yet not enough of an improvement to raise it rating on BGG.  For you only make one decision each round, stay or go. And that's not enough to hold my interest for long. Yes, its just a 
filler. But I've played many fillers with much more going on, that make them 
hold up over repeated play. So my rating of "5" stands. 
- 03/21/17 I played one more 5P game of Incan Gold. 
Around this time the Incan Gold entry on BGG was merged into the Diamant entry, as they are virtually the same game. Alas all my above comments and rating then went Poof!.  Only I didn't know that until November. 
- 11/22/17 I did my best to recreate them.
- 11/23/17 Now my collections shows two Diamant entries. I blame the BGG Admins continuing to do loopy things with Incan Gold / Diamant.  Akk! So I deleted the oldest one.

RATING: 7
18 oct 07 Essen buying spree
Initial rating: Nice little "push your luck" filler. Fun if you're into that. Fast gameplay, good for starters or just a quick game. Definitely not a gamer's game, but good in bigger groups, the more the merrier, and the harder it gets to win on tactics...

Update after lots of plays: this one is definitely a winner with "non-gamers".

RATING: 5
[size=10][u][i][b]r{Initial Thoughts}r (after 5 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* Lavishly produced press-your-luck game
* Excellent with more, and can be a raucously good time with the right group
* Game takes about 5 minutes to teach with no downtime
* Those who never leave can upset the game's balance, but usually finish first or last
* Good for lighter gamers, large groups and press-your luck fans
* Initial rating: [b]8/10[/b]

[size=10][u][i][b]b{Further Thoughts}b (after 25 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* Like most games, has burnout potential if played too often
* Lack of any deep decisions make this a beginning/end of game day filler at best 
* Plays have slowed quite a bit, but this still has a permanent home in the collection
* Further rating: [b]6/10[/b]

[size=10][u][i][b]g{Advanced Thoughts}g (after 50 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* At 50+ plays, feeling of burnout is strong
* Only one real choice in the game (should I stay or should I go?)
* Lighter design means that some will want to play this over...and over...and over
* Advanced rating: [b]5/10[/b]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Diamant is a simple "push-your-luck" game where players play adventurers seeing gems and riches in five different mines. Each turn, players decide whether they want to continue the expedition and delve further into the mine or bail out and leave with whatever treasure they have acquired thus far. Of course, it wouldn't be fun if there wasn't any danger involved. There are hazards in the mines as well. There are scorpions, snakes, poison gas, cave-ins and explosions that the brave explorers will encounter. If players are in the mine after two of the same hazard cards come up then they die and lose any gems they have acquired.

This game is quite simple and plays fairly quick. It's easy to explain and is quite exciting to play. It definitely surpassed my expectation of a game with such a simple mechanic. Players susceptible to trying to push their luck will find this game a lot of fun and entertaining. No deep strategies involved, however decisions will sometimes get tough. Recommended for a light, filler type game that produces lot of laughs.

RATING: 6
Push your luck for most treasure.

Plays: A couple.
Type: VP race = a game where you race to collect victory points (fastest/most).
Complexity: Family game = a game that is easy to teach and play.
# of players: See BGG.
Playing time: See BGG.
Player interaction: Competition for unlimited resources.
Randomness: Medium – card draw, but cards affect all players equally.

Replayability: High. It’s very quick so why not go again?
Fun: Definitely. Each step into the temple is exciting. Tension rises as more threats are revealed. Getting away with the artifacts is fun. Timing your exit just before the temple collapses is fun.
Memorability: Low, it’s a VP race that doesn’t create stories.

Thematic integration: Decent. The art does a good job communicating the theme.
Components: Pretty! Very good for such a cheap game. The player tents are a nice touch.

Who will like this: Large families.

RATING: 6
Fun, quick push your luck game for up to 8 players. Feels almost party game-ish.

Getting diminishing returns with this one. Sometimes the cards come up in such a way that things are not very interesting. Games often have at least one round where everyone's in the temple with 2 or 3 gems when the second disaster hits. Also when someone jumps out to a lead, the game gets formulaic and stale as the decisions become obvious: Got a big lead? Play it safe. Far behind? Well, you've gotta play it risky. At this point players are simply at the mercy of the cards.

There are still games of Incan Gold that are fun and filled with tension, but they are infrequent.

RATING: 5.5
Short, fairly random push-your-luck game. The rewards of risky play generally outweigh the consequences of losing your bet, just because they are so large (getting a 15-gem card and not having to divvy it up with anyone is great!).

That said, the game feels like it could have used more careful design that didn't make a lot of the expeditions frustrating or pointless: it's just not fun having a bunch of trap cards turn up right at the start, quickly terminating the trip. Too often, play becomes automatic (e.g. say you draw a low-value gem card then a series of traps--there's literally no point where any player has an incentive to turn back, so it's a bunch of automatic "continue" votes and then a bomb when the 2nd trap is drawn). Every so often there's an amazing high-risk adventure where people gradually drop out and someone keeps pushing their luck--but that's not as often as I'd like. -- Also this is one of those games where there is perfect information that is half-disguised by keeping winnings out of sight, so anyone who can track the winnings will often be playing on auto-pilot in the last round since they know exactly how many points everyone needs to win.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.8
Video Review: https://youtu.be/L3xOX_VJN2w

Diamant is the quintessential push your luck game. Adventures head into a cave and face traps, treasure or relics, which are shown on cards. After each card is revealed, adventure take any required actions and decide whether to carry on, or leave. If they leave on their own they can collect any relics that have been uncovered and all remaining treasure, if they leave with others then relics are left and the remaining loot is split equally. Why would you leave? Well the first time you see a trap of a certain type you are ok, but if that trap type comes out again you flee the cave and get nothing! Including treasure you have already collected on that run! Awesome little game with great components including cardboard treasure chests to store your banked treasures in!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A push your luck filler in the same box size as the Kosmos 2-Player collection. 

Each turn the players must decide if they will push deeper into the temple in search of greater fortune or pull out in the hope of getting a share of the spoils, which is only possible if those that push on end up coming to grieve.

Coming to grieve occurs when a danger card is drawn. There are several types of danger cards in the deck and pulling one of these of a certain type is fine if it is the first...but not if it is the second of its type.

Thus the game is revealed...the players have limited information but are never sure of what is lurking around the next corner!

The game is played over a series of 5 rounds, one for each level of the temple. 

A really clever game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.7
主題:1
利用冒險尋寶，面對未知的陷阱來考驗人性貪婪的主題性強烈遊戲，主題與遊戲規則能相呼應。

美術:0.6
本遊戲是個小品遊戲，盒子外殼很厚，外加寶石籌碼是實物不是紙板，還算可取之處。美工及其他的部分只能說堪稱及格。

規則:1
規則簡單，好講解，小朋友一聽就懂，基本上就是一個字"賭"，賭運氣、賭膽識，不過喜歡策略的人可能會覺得沒有深度。
遊戲過程就是先看看場面上發現的寶石有多少，玩家決定要不要返回營地，獲得自己的寶石；或者決定繼續冒險，贏取更多寶藏，又或者發先災難空手而回。就怎麼簡單。

設置:1 好設置，洗一洗冒險牌庫，每人各發一張前進或者後退的卡片就好了。是入門遊戲中好教學好設置的遊戲。

路線:0.2
本遊戲路線只有兩種，前進或後退。難怪大人會不喜歡，但是小孩超愛。不過要玩的有深度，勉強可以將災難卡的發生率放進決策過程中，或許可以增加一點遊戲深度。

互動:1
本遊戲在路線上得分落後，但是在玩家互動中得到最高分，假如真的拿這款遊戲來賭錢，我想連大人都會被這款遊戲征服。遊戲中的互動產生在大家返回營地時拿取的寶石或者是神器，每一個抉擇，都考驗著人性。

個人:0.4
剛開開這款遊戲，覺得很刺激，但隨著開的次數越多，越覺得本款遊戲深度不足，個人只有在推廣桌遊時，當作推抗工具。除非真的玩錢，不然個人不會為想玩這個遊戲而開。

朋友:0.7
小朋友絕對愛的遊戲，每次小孩開這款遊戲都很投入，大人反應普普。

想玩:0.2
沒有深度，只能教入門。

收藏:0.6
雖然個人覺得本遊戲不夠深度，但做為推廣桌遊的遊戲，這款遊戲倒是很棒，另外賭博的機制也是桌遊少見的遊戲方式，看在價格上還是可以收藏。

總分:6.7
講評:本遊戲反應兩極，就看個人的喜愛程度了。

RATING: 7
Quick and enjoyable; easy-to-learn push your luck game
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Deck of 30 cards composed of 15 disasters (five different types, three cards each) and fifteen numbers ranging from 1 to 17. In a round, flip a card. If it is a number card, all explorers present split the gems; if it is a disaster card, no one is in danger unless it is the second copy of the same disaster. Everyone then loses their gems. Players have the option of retreating back to base camp before the next card is drawn and splitting the leftover gems left on cards, and having the privilege of banking their gems. Play over five rounds. A cute little game that plays quickly. If you gamble and win, it's fun, if you lose, it's still fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Reprint of Diamant, where players are adventurerers, trying to get treasure and avoid disasters. The difference from Diamant is that there is a reward for being the only one to leave first. 

It`s a light, fun, push your luck game. Good for closing out a session, and plays quickly in 20 minutes.

RATING: 6.5
While this game uses a push-your-luck system like Can't Stop, I would recommend Diamant if you're the shady sort of gamer who, (like yours truly) prefers a thick coating of theme. While not an elaborate theme by any means; you're exploring these 5 caves for gems, as you advance, dangers may befall you and if you should encounter more than 1 danger, you must retreat from that cave and lose all gems collected - it does work. There's a tangible satisfaction which accompanies plonking  the pretty gem bits in your little old-skool shipping container. There just is. 

Another fun thing about this game is that cowards can win big! Running before everyone else out of the cave means that you collect all the gems that were rounded out during distribution when going into the cave. Perfect if there's someone cocky that you'd like to humble, hee.

RATING: 4
A very simple Push-Your-Luck game. Temple turn cards and tents are an effort to give this game some more value and distract players from the fact that all you really are doing is giving a single yes/no answer each turn. This same game could be played with pennies and a regular deck of cards.

The turquoise treasure pieces look like Gushers fruit snacks, so if you are looking, over the course of the game you will catch players eying them hungrily.

After trying this, No Thanks!, and For Sale, I think I want more out of my games than these light fillers. There is just not enough 'game' to them.

RATING: 7.4
Diamant is a very basic push your luck game that can be learnt in one minute and played in 10. It's been deprived of all the accessory to provide a pure push your luck experience.

The production is good. The art is mediocre, but the boxes and gems are great (even if sometimes there are not enough of them).

But the gameplay is really fun. It's luck, but your decisions are very important. There's a mathematical basis in all the decisions, but the decisions of the other players will matter almost as much, and they are simultaneous.

First impression [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/184429/item/4194325#item4194325]here[/url].

RATING: 6.9
Great game for complete non-gamers. Also good for children...if their parents have no objections to teaching little kids light gambling.

Good for teaching division as well.

We play the following variant:
If a card with gems is revealed, all the gems are piled onto that card; they are NOT divided up and piled up outside everyone's tents.

You only get gems if you decide to leave, at which point you divide up all of the gems that are in the temple so far. Now the question changes from, "Should I keep my (a+b+c)/n?" to "If I leave now, what will k be in (a+b+c)/k?"

I'm not sure if this is better, but this game isn't strategic anyway. This is a filler.

RATING: 8
[b]Diamant[/b] was traded away in a math trade 2/15/17. (Received Citrus)
Was received in a trade (12/10/14)

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]Originally owned Incan gold but the component quality was just okay. The card quality was not that good, and the fold up tents stunk. Also every game we played multiple people would get confused with the cards used to show whether you were leaving or staying. I ended up trading Incan Gold and got a copy of [thing=15512][/thing]. This has remained one of our go to push your luck games, especially when we have friends and family over.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- Fun, quick filler that plays up to 8. 
- This game is easy to teach/learn; we have brought this to family get togethers and had a lot of fun playing with our extended families. 
- This game can be an addictive push your luck game. 
- The components for Diamant are absolutely amazing (diamonds for the gems, cool boxes for the gems and little Indiana Jones meeples)[/i].

RATING: 7
A worthy 20 min push-your-luck play-the-odds filler for large crowds of 6 to 8. We've moved to the 'balls of steel' variant, where all gems stay on the mines (ie not evenly distributed), which has produced much more groan and hilarity. There's more importance on out-guessing the other players now rather than the cards. Anyway, it's still coming out occasionally after all these years because it's a niche winner.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A remake of Diamant so it gets the same rating as the original, in that it's a worthy 20min push-your-luck play-the-odds filler, especially for larger crowds of 6 to 8. We usually employ the 'balls of steel' variant, where all gems stay on the mines (ie not evenly distributed), which has produced much groan and hilarity, and places more importance on out-guessing the other players now rather than the cards. This edition is probably better than the original because of the addition of artifacts which, when they appear, offer 5pts to anyone who manages to pull out when no one else does. Which obviously gives more to double-out-think-yourself over.

RATING: 7
A very simple, light, fun game about wending your way through old Incan temples in search of treasure and artifacts.  The rules will take maybe five minutes to explain and the entire game less than an hour no matter how many players you throw at it.

Again, no deep strategy, but good for adults, kids, maybe even very intelligent pets.  Simple, fun filler as you wait for the pizza to arrive or the next big game to get rolling.

This is a light push-your-luck-style filler game.  Its main advantage is that it can accommodate up to eight players without bogging down at all.  That said, it accomplishes this via simultaneous action selection, which isn't my favorite mechanic.  It's light, it's fun, it can take a lot of people, so it definitely has a niche.

RATING: 7
(10+ plays)  A push your luck game where turns are simultaneous.  Great design!  A few too many games have fallen flat, so I'm not sure how long this one will last.  Some games are a nail biting game of chicken, with tough decisions and dramatic reveals.  Can be a total blast!  Other games can be so anti-climatic, especially if multiple rounds are really bad luck.

"Reveal first card of first round.  Spider.  Second card.   Zombie.  Third card. Cave-In.  Fourth card.  Zombie.  OK.  We've been chased out of the temple by zombies.  So we go to round 2."
new players... stunned
"Wait, what just happened?"
"Um, well, that's not normal, just hang with me here...."
When the whole game goes nearly this bad (and some do)... it is hard to recover the new players to let them see the magic this game can be.

RATING: 8
A great, simple "push your luck" game where players take their turns simultaneously (no down-time between turns).
Inter-player interaction is on the low side from a mechanics stand point, but there is a LOT of interaction in the form of psyching each other out with, "I'm leaving this turn. I swear! You don't believe me?".

This game goes great with beer... cause that's usually how we've played it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
On order from GameSurplus - June 4 06
Arrived - June 14th.  Great service from these guys. www.gamesurplus.com

Update:  Upon further inspection, I realized that the game did not come with a starting mat.  I wrote to the publisher, who was very prompt in shipping a replacement mat to me overseas.  Thanks for excellent service!

Update:  I keep bringing this game to social functions, thinking that /someone/ will get excited about the neat bits and quick gameplay.. but noone seems interested!  Gah!  I WILL PLAY THIS GAME.

Update:  I did.  No matter how many people dog this game, it will always be a superb one for me.  In truth, it is extremely overproduced, but it's exactly that which makes it so desireable.  It's a fun push-your-luck game that can be taught in 10 minutes and played in the same (depending on how familiar you are with the basics).  I've found Diamant to be an excellent game to teach to new players, and can also be a great compliment to beer n' pretzels nights as there's really no serious thought required to play it.  Simple, pleasing to the eye, fast, and unique - and that's why I like it so much.

Update:  Get Diamant while you still can!!  Is it only available in German?  Who cares!?  Get it.  Incan Gold may be cheaper, but it's the remake.. the original is the best here, folks.

As such this removes any speculative skill in deciding to progress or pull out and what I feel is the nagging conviction that luck undermines any deliberation. (This problem is highlighted when playing Zirkus Flocahti, a similar push your luck game whereby you go through the deck once, is more forgiving and which I'd much rather play with 4 than Diamant). 

The sitting out a la Cloud 9 bothers me alittle too as there is nothing active for the spectators to do except watch the sitcom. Diamant seems best with more than 4 as the divisions are smaller and there are richer pickings left behind. As with Hick Hack and Wyatt Earp there is that Jackpot payout which is wonderful drama. Yes I agree that the game is expensive for what it is, but I've yet to be convinced there is any better non-party filler for more than 5 players with little downtime.

RATING: 7
A nice, quick playing push your luck game, where it's almost entirely player driven. Everyone secretly chooses to stay or go, then simultaneously reveal their cards. Players who leave the temple by themselves before the dangers kill everyone win big, players who leave a the same time win medium. Players eaten by disasters win nothing. Game is played over several rounds, so hopefully falling behind at the wrong time isn't devastating.

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:nostar: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:nostar: Multiple plays stay interesting
:star: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::star::nostar: Raw enjoyment

RATING: 7
Incan Gold is a classic filler game based on the "push your luck" mechanism. About the same level of complexity as For Sale, Incan Gold can also be a good gateway game provided there are at least 4-6 players. The game plays upto 8, but I suspect it may be a bit chaotic with 8 players. The game lasts about 20-25 minutes (if all players know the rules) and there isn't much scope for AP as the decision on each turn is limited to 2 simple options - either continue exploring the ruins or get out with whatever treasure you've already collected.

RATING: N/A
I own the Eagle/Gryphon Incan Gold edition. A very simple push your luck game that works pretty well with children and muggles both. It has the right amount of risk aversion and rooting for your opponents to fail. It's more or less a way to collect treasure, divided by the number of players left in the expedition. So you have an incentive to be the last one remaining, though if two threats are revealed that are the same, you go bust. So it's the same tension you'd get in many other PYL games, but that doesn't make it less fun.

RATING: 8
great filler that plays quickly and generates a lot of laughs. non-gamers are impressed with the quality of the bits-the indiana jones meeples are pretty fun, not to mention the jewels and treasure crates. anyway, one problem  with the press your luck genre, at least for me, is that player interaction is usually pretty thin if not non-existent.  with diamant, the simultaneous action selection adds a nice element of bluffing and second guessing, which gets players to react to each other, which is all you need in a game this light. i also like how the odds change as the game progresses and how the game uses cards instead of dice. there's not much to this game, and even the new edition is still kind of pricey, but f' it: you're probably just going to spend the money you'd spend on this on something else just as frivolous, or temporal, so just pick it up if you want it.

RATING: 7
How simple is this game!  
I first played it with a group of 5, one of which is slightly game-phobic.  However, when I explained that the only decision to be made on each turn is "stay" or "leave", the phobia fell away.  
Despite the simplicity of the decision to make, this is a really fun game of pushing your luck: the longer you stay in the mine, the more gems you could get, the bigger the risk of hazards & leaving with nothing.  
We ended up playing four complete games in a row because it's so quick yet compulsive.  On mines where everyone got out before falling to hazards, everyone wanted the cards to be continued just to see how far they could have gone!
An great game that is definitely suitable for even the most game-wary friends, and demands a replay.

RATING: 7.5
Incan gold is an inexpensive push your luck game.  I enjoy its quick play time and the fact it can support up to 8 players if needed.  The treasure pieces and "tents" are nicely produced and the cards feel sturdy.

This game was a big hit with my family - the theme went over well, it was fun seeing if someone lost all their take for the round due to some disaster, and it played fast so that the kids never lost interest.  In fact, after playing twice my youngest asked if we could play a third time!

The game is rather simplistic, but I think thats part of its appeal.  A lot of fun for not a lot of money - very glad I bought it.

RATING: 6.45
A clever little game, essentially modelled around old fashioned gambling games. Players delve ever deeper into a mine sharing any gems found. If players fold they no longer claim a share, if they press on to long hazards close the mine and they lose everything. There is some nerve involved in holding as long as you should, a little psychology in picking the right moment to pull out, and a certain amount of counting in keeping track of the other players scores. Light fun that could easily pass an evening with the right group of players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Incan Gold is  a simple push your luck game. Five times you and the other players enter a temple. One card at a time treasures (or disasters are revealed). Each time you take your share and choose to press on or run. If too many disasters strike the expedition is lost.
Its quite fun and easy to teach, I would consider it as a good gateway game to introduce those new to boardgames. It is less useful to fill a short time for gamers. It takes a little bit too long. And the dominant strategy is counting. Players treasure are hidden but you know all of the inputs and outputs so you ought to be able to calculate it. And in my experience want that from a light game.
