RATING: 7
I cannot imagine a more elegant version of this game.  Every rule feels organic, as if the game grew naturally from good soil.  If, for the next 10 years, I never look at this game again, I will still be able to recite the rules from memory.  That's how natural and obvious the rules are.

Considering how superficially easy it is to teach, there is a surprising amount to it.  It fits a very specific but useful niche in my collection--something to pull out during parties, when 5-10 people (maybe even more, and certainly including children and non-gamers) are willing to devote as little as 15 minutes for a game (and that includes rules explanations).  

The fun is watching the band of explorers slowly chicken out.  The chickens hope the daredevils get their just desserts, and vice versa. The larger the group, the bigger the risk/reward payoff, and the more laughter/ooohs/aaaahs.  It's a thoughtful party game where no-one has to pantomime, show off their drawing skills, or do any other potentially embarrassing action.

Despite all that's good about it, Incan Gold/Diamant is still a one-note filler game.  There is only one decision to be made over and over again--given the probability of death in the next room (a value which can be easily calculated), should I continue or retreat safely with my treasure?  Each decision is basically  identical to the next.  Each game is basically identical to the next.  But the game serves its purpose well, which is to generate laughter/ooohs/aaahs from your friends and family.

PS.  I own Incan Gold.  Diamant looks better, but is considerably more expensive.  Incan Gold art is too dark.  Creepy child zombie art feels out of place for this kind of light game.  Almost all components have been made from playing cards, even the components that would be better made out of things other than playing cards (specifically, the "go/no go" cards and the money tents).  But oh well, for the price, it's still a good deal.

RATING: 5
Diamant somewhat lost its luster over time. I still enjoy it, but the fun-factor is not nearly as high as, say, Liar's dice, another entry in the accessible, high-player-count, party-game department. An absurdly early cave-in can happen from time to time, which feels somewhat dissatisfying. 

It certainly plays better at high player counts, because players are incentivized to delve deeper to avoid sharing the riches. Higher player counts also make the decision to take or ignore relics feel much more impactful. However, the pure push-your-luck nature lacks the competitive punch I seek in most games. It does not betray its purpose in that regard, and remains a commendable filler.

(+) Light rules overhead and quick to teach and play.
(+) IELLO version in particular as high production quality. The components are vibrant, the boxes are sturdy, and overall the game is visually appealing.
(+) Works even better at higher player counts.

(-) Almost -too- simple. Push-your-luck is all that it offers.
(-) It is a bit too random at times. Bad luck can be jarring when it ends the fun spelunking phase too early.
(-) Shallow gameplay already made me feel like it lacks longevity, though I can see it retaining novelty if left unplayed for a while.

RATING: 8
09-09-2014. Reratings after 7 plays. I still rate the game highly (8). My go to filler.

29-05-2014. Rated after 1 play with 4. I recently acquired a second-hand -but as new- copy of Diamant. 

In Diamant you play adventurers aiming to get most loot/treasure/jewels from a dangerous cave with a host of dangers as possible. You do this by flipping cards from a deck of 30 cards to symbolize exploring the cave. This temple deck consists out of 5 sets of 3 danger cards and 15 jewel cards of various denominations. 

For each treasure card flipped, you equally divide the number of jewels across the adventurers. If a few jewels cannot be divided, they are put on the card to be picked up later. Before the next card is flipped, each player chooses secretly to continue or leave the cave. If the player chooses to leave, he picks up all remaining treasures. If several choose to leave at the same time, they divide remaining treasures equally and safely store their loot outside of the cave.

If the players push on, the next card if flipped. If the flipped card is a danger card, and an identical danger card was already revealed everyone still inside dies and gets no treasure.

After 5 rounds, the one with most safely stored jewels is the winner.

I really like this game. It's a simple push your luck-type filler that plays up to 8, in about 20 minutes. Regardless, the game offers some challenge and you have to predict what other people are going to do (flee or push) and if you still dare to continue given the amount of danger / amount of jewels you already have. In short, yes, it's a simple game, but it's incredibly fun, elicits laughter and just makes for an excellent time..

RATING: 7
A classic press your luck game.  It's fun, it's re-playable, and I can see it being popular with different groups of friends.

The bits that are provided with the game come in eye-catching colors (gold, onyx, and a beautiful turquoise) and the artwork is nice.

Cons: The system to hide your "banked" points is flimsy and not protective enough.  After a while, the system to decide whether you will press your luck or not gets repetitive and annoying.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Half the reason I like this game is the presentation. I'm known to salvage coloured gems from other games just to add to the bling factor.

Underneath is a pretty good push-your-luck game. Dropping/not dropping your adventurer kinda slows the game down, but I do it to enhance the drama. Leaving a trail of the indivisible gems is great because it gives people incentive to leave early due to gain, in addition to the fear of loss from the traps.

I actually had a disappointing first play of the game and spent some time crunching the statistics. Now I strongly recommend that people play with only 2 of each trap card (or require that all 3 need to be revealed). The deck is surprisingly trap-heavy, so this helps to prevent anti-climaxes. It also makes each successive cave more lucrative (and therefore fun!), since you're removing an entire trap each time you die.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
A favorite for over a decade. Push you luck doesn't get any better than this, IMO. Sure, Can't Stop exists, but this has that little dross of theme which kicks it up a level. I've never had this one fail, and I think I need both hands to count how many non-gamers I've made REALLY excited about boardgaming with this one.

I like to play up the tension, draw out the choices. he miners don't die, they run screaming from the mine dropping all of their jewels, if I play with my kids.

It's too terrible to contemplate playing with the crappy-componented American version. inca gold or something? I shudder at how much worse it feels than this one. Played once, never again. Spend the money on an Amazon.de order. It's worth it!

RATING: 7.4
Fun push-your-luck game that can be played with up to 8 people. A fixed part of my 'party game collection' from now on! The mechanics are really easy: "will you venture deeper into the cave: Y/N?" That's all there is to it, and therefore the game is easy to explain, quick to learn and the luck-based system actually gives every player at the table a chance to come out on top.

Iello's edition gives it beautiful artwork and shiny components, making this already quick-to-grasp game all the more easy to get through to people and onto the table.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
The popularity of this game around my house has been a very pleasant surprise.  The idea behind the game is really quite simple -- how far are you willing to push your luck?  But there is analysis that can be put into that.  What are the rewards for leaving against possible penalties for staying?  Do you need to make up ground?  What is the likelihood of a detrimental draw?  Against that, you can do well playing solely from your gut -- something my daughters do quite well.  That levels the playing field in a manner that allows them to beat daddy, which is something they find endless enjoyment in.  Perhaps its popularity here should not be so surprising after all :)  [02/02/2008]

RATING: 7
Own both Diamant and Incan Gold --

Diamant -- Played 3 through 8 players.  Enjoyed every time.  Treasure chests and Indiana Jones-shaped meeples!  Fun in a party atmosphere or as a filler.  The "Diamant Jones and the Forbidden Idol" variant brings some nail-biting tension to the game -- When a player gets the idol, it makes for a lot of noise, and when players try but fail, the frustrated hopes are palpable.

Incan Gold -- Artifacts and three denominations of gems made this worth checking out.

Incan Diamant -- The best components and elements of both games!

RATING: 8
Played 1 3P game of this. A very simple, quick yet engaging game where players are exploring an ancient temple and encountering treasures and hazards along the way. The only decision you are going to make throughout the game is to press on or stop. If players recklessly plunge headlong, they can be either rewarded with plenty of gold, or lose everything they have gathered so far. At the same time, deciding to go back is not so easy, as the number of players who turn back at the same time can influence the amount of treasure picked up. A fantastic filler!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
2016: 7. A fun light push-your-luck filler game that plays well regardless of the number of players.  Wins can be swingy 'cuz the game involves so much luck, but I don't mind it at all.  For me it's all about the laughs and second guessing and "rolling of the dice" to see if you can get just that little bit more out of the cave than anyone else!

Played this game with my nieces and nephew (7, 5 and 3) and they totally got what was going on. (Pro tip: get little bowls for the kiddies instead of the tents, your jewels won't go flying all over the place) And I think that's where the game shines: a light, fun family game that plays a lot of people and you can have a great time regardless of your age or gaming experience.  Gamer-gamers should probably look for other options.

2017: 8. I think this is my go to party/kids/everybody filler game.  Plays a lot, plays quick, people don't have to think, and it plays all ages.  It's perfect.

P:3-8

RATING: 6
Diamant is a very simple game of "push your luck". There are five turns in the game, each one consisting of a few to several rounds. In each round, each player decides before time whether s/he wishes to be "in" or "out". Then a card is revealed. If the card is a treasure card, all "in" players get an equal share of the booty. There are (I think) 15 treasure cards. Leftover treasure sits on the card. If it is an artifact card, nothing happens. If it is a hazard card, and the first of its type, nothing happens. (There are 3 each of 5 different hazard cards, if I recall.) If the revealed card is the *second* hazard of a given type - that is, one has already been revealed this round - then all players who are "in" LOSE all the treasure they have accumulated in the round so far. So as you play deeper into a round, and more hazards appear, you must decide whether staying "in" (and the chance of getting even more treasure) justifies the possibility of losing everything. As soon as you decide to go "out" (return to camp), then you and any other departures travel back along the cards already revealed, splitting any leftover treasure sitting there. Also, if ONLY on person leaves, and an artifact has been revealed, that player gets to claim the artifact as his own. When you go "out" you place your treasure (in the Incan Gold version) under you card tent, and you cannot lose it. It's yours until the end of the game.

Diamant/Incan Gold is a very simple game with two prominent elements: 1) figuring your odds based upon deck composition and what has already been revealed, and 2) bluffing your opponents/doing the unexpected. You must balance (1) with (2) to win. You have to make prudent decisions, but you also (ideally) would like to see the other players chickening out and leaving you to get all the treasure, or conversely: you bail out when the time is right, and they lose everything.

This game gets much better with more players, which makes it a nice party game. It also seems great for kids, as the mechanics are simple, there is basic math (learning is fun!), there is good tension, and it's fun! But it isn't a very satisfying game for me. That is to say, it's a filler. It's a *good* filler, but I don't generally think filler games are the bees' knees. Even so, I would recommend this game to pretty much anybody, simply because it is so good as a filler and because anyone can play.

RATING: 10
I'm rating this as a game for 5 year olds! 

And up of course, but really, my rating is for this being a game that an adult can really play with a 5yo and both enjoy themselves. How rare is that?! So yes, I'm rating it as a family game, but specifically as a game for 5yos, because there are too few good games for the 3-5yo set.

My 5yo absolutely loves Incan Gold, and the 6yo neighbor girl visits us specifically requesting Incan Gold. To top it all off, Incan Gold teaches them adding, and introduces adding 5's and 10's. And that just sneaks up on them without them really noticing it. The first maybe 10 plays we counted out the gold & jewels to go on the cards, but after a while they took over, asking if they did it correctly. They WANTED to learn it - how great is that?! My kid is now soon 6 and the girl soon 7, but we still have to count who won. But if you want kids to do it on their own, you just use the 1-point jewels, that way they can count them easier, or just measure stacks.

The art may be too scary for some 5yos. If your kid is prone to nightmares, I'd wait a while with Ican Gold. We had to un-scarify the zombie by just referring her as "oh no, it's that scary old lady". ("Undead" would definitely be too much ... :-D) But then the rest was ok. 

I will be gifting Incan Gold to well-balanced non-traumatized secure-in-themselves 5yos in the future.

My only gripe would be that I wish the gold & jewels were as pretty as the ones in Diamant.

Thank you, Funagain Games, for printing this!

RATING: 8
This is a nice filler game, that sadly is not worth the high price-tag.  I like the system, but I kind of feel this social push your luck element was better done in the original FX Schmidt Cloud 9 (not the Out of the Box version).  Nonetheless, it plays with more players than Cloud 9 and is quick and simple to explain to large groups.

There is certainly something to the game, luck is prevelant but there are some decisions to it that have their own repercussions.   The thing that makes this game unique is the decision of when to bail.  Timing is essential on when to pick up the jewels on your way out of the cave.  It is good fun, when you want a lucky filler.  

Update:  The new version doesn't have the original board, so now it's affordable.  Well worth the price, a great game, and a great buy.

RATING: 6
This seems to be a good little game for kids or non-gamers, as well as a simple little filler for a larger group.  Although I find it becomes stale pretty quickly, it has been very well received by most people I have introduced it to, largely, I think, due to its simplicity and to the tension built into the "push your luck" mechanic (which is all this game really is).  For myself, there is just too little to the game to keep me interested.  But having said that, for what it is, it is very well produced.  Although my edition didn't come with the game board (which is not at all necessary), it does have a lot of neat bits what with all the gems, the treasure boxes, and the little wooden explorers.  One advantage of this game is that it can be played with up to 8 people, although if I were looking for a simple game to play with a larger group I'd be more inclined to pull out a party game.  And I wouldn't really recommend playing with less than four due to the decreased amount of competition in an already fairly dry game.  Game design: 4/5  Personal enjoyment: 2/5  Total: 6/10

RATING: 4.5
Good push-your-luck filler. Turn over a card, either treasure or a hazard. Players simultaneously choose whether to leave the temple (splitting treasure found so far) or stay. A second hazard of the same type means those remaining get nothing.

An excellent example of the genre, perhaps the very best because it plays briskly even with more players, but not one I have any interest in. If Ra involves too much luck for my taste, you can guess what I think about Incan Gold. I'd rather play the "have a conversation" filler.

RATING: 6.5
Based on a number of plays. I have mostly played with kids but sometimes with adults or a mixture.  The kids (ages 4 - 7) liked the game.  The 4 year olds understand the rules and the game's pace is fast enough to keep their attention.  However, they do not quite have a competitive level of strategy and are not able make good choices.  The 7 year old caught on pretty fast and can play it well.  The adults in general have not overly excited about the game, and impression I got was "hmm... decent kids game".  None of the adults were eager to replay it right away.  I would probably give it about a 5 or 6 myself,  my kids would probably give it a 8 or so, so I blend the rating to be 7 for my family.  Dropped it to a 6.5 because the replay value is less than I initially thought for both kids and adults.  Still an okay game, but can be repetitive if played enough times.

RATING: 6.5
[Schmidt Spiele 'Diamant' first edition with the board] {Treasure hunt, beers&pretzels, gateway; luck-pressing, simultaneous-action; optimal 6-8p} Diamant is a pleasant party game with nice player interaction. It is suitable for all kinds of players. It's funny to see that everyone retreats while you are the only one choose to stay :laugh: and everyone yelling disaster / gem.

The pawns, treasure create and diamonds are very beautiful and attractive. Maybe, these excellent bits make the game unfairly expensive. USD39.95 is really too much for this simple party game. I am lucky to have a copy of the first edition. Although the board, pawns and crates are not necessary to play the game, Diamant is more enjoyable with it.

[Update] I am not convinced by the Incan Gold edition. The original bits are cool. Even though there are new rules, I stick to Diamant.

RATING: 9
Marvelous little family game. Elegant and restrained. The exploration theme works well too. Push your fellow explorers to move further into the cave while you sneak off and scoop up the leftovers. Someone else mentioned that this was Can't Stop + Adel. Couldn't have said it better myself. Bravo!

Rating moved from an 8 to a 9 after playing it in person. We played three times in a row and laughed uproariously each time. My favorite so far for 2005!

Update: Finally played the "Incan Gold" version. Not bad at all and a nice new scoring variation that's not possible to play with the original. Still, I'm fine with the original and feel no real need to upgrade. However, If you don't have the original, INCAN GOLD is a MUST PURCHASE.

RATING: 7
A recent, but solid addition to my collection. Incan Gold is a very easy game to teach and plays very quickly. It is essentially a “press-your luck” game where you may guarantee your winnings, but those who dare to go farther may get more riches or lose them all. You play five rounds so you might get nothing in one round, but manage to win it all by doing well on the others. Before each turn you flip either a camp (leave the temple, but keep what you have found) or torch (can get more riches, but risk losing everything from that round).  The cards and gems are very nice quality and come in a small box which is easy to store. The tents where you place your winnings inside, to hide the total from everyone else are also pretty cool!

My only complaint is that the torch and camp cards are a little too similar…

RATING: 8
Incan Gold (US variant): Plus: artifact cards (artifacts come out and the game gets very strange). Minuses: cards are standard-size and don't form a maze, so a Diamant-style layout can get too big for a small table. Mixed: Tents aren't as nice as treasure chests, but are more secretive; the continue/run-away cards aren't as nice as the meeples and the run-away card can get misplaced, but some players like the idea that they can randomized the cards and their choice; the lumps of faux touquise, obsidian, and gold aren't as nice as the rubies and diamonds, but more--enough--are in the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
About the only good thing to say about Incan Gold is it's so simple, children can play it and everyone will still have a good time.

Here's my problem with the game. Because your personal "guaranteed money" stack is small compared to the money on the track, you have no good choices. If you leave, someone else will leave with you, so you won't get the artifacts and you'll have to split what's on the track. If you stay, the people who left will clear the track, which means for the next few rounds you'll have nothing to gain by leaving yourself. By the time it's worth leaving again, either you'll have hit two matching disasters and get nothing, or leaving will still be a bad choice.

Games like Can't Stop, or even "Deal or No Deal," are more interesting because it's quite easy to build up your earnings to the point where you have something significant to gain by stopping, which means you have something to gain by going on as well. So there are two good choices, which is a much funner position to be in than Incan Gold's two bad choices, which are just not fun at all.

RATING: 8
One of the best press-your-luck games, Incan Gold is simple, thematic, and downright stressful as you push your adventurer deeper into the caves, hoping you won't be crushed, burned, eaten alive, or murdered by cannibal pygmies before escaping with a fistful of gems. The components here are a bit flimsy (especially compared to the pricier Diamant), but definitely worth a spot in every collection due to its easy rules, ability to work with a large number of players, and fast and fun gameplay.

[b]Player Count Verdict: 5+[/b]
The game needs more players to be interesting. That way you never know who is going to run out early and grab an artifact, and who is going to stay in until the end.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Definitely plays better as you increase players. In fact my rating would go up .5 or one point if I only played with 6-8 players.

Why are the "Stay" and "Leave" cards so similar. Every game it seems as though someone picks the wrong card accidentally. Why can't one be all dark and tomb-y and the other be bright and outside-y?

Plays up to eight people over a wide age range in less than 30 minutes and takes up very little space (packed up or on the table).  For a gamer who travels this is pretty special.




Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 5
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 5
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 5
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 5


Overall - 5

RATING: 8
A filler hit! Fun, fast push-your-luck kind of game. Easy to teach and, even with 6 (the most I have played) all is said and done in about 20 minutes.

There is only two things to do:
1 - Decide if you want to stay in the search for treasures or return to camp;
2 - Turn over the next search card.

Sure, there is reasons to return (take what was left in the cards passed and the artifacts) and to continue (gain more treasure), but if the second hazard of the same type appear, bad luck! Everyone still in the search lose everything.

Really good game!

My review (in portuguese) is [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/851054/incan-gold-resenha-em-portugues-review-in-portug]here[/url].

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Incan Gold Edition - relatively simple card game for up to 8 players (explorers) venturing into an Incan Temple all trying to amass the biggest cache of gems & artifacts and return them to the safety of their camps. There are 5 Quests (rounds) per game each of which has 15 'Quest' (Good)cards and 15 'Hazard' (Bad) cards, with anything from 1 to 5 artifacts also thrown in for good measure. These all form the 'Quest' draw pile that is used each round to determine what the explorers find as they venture into the Temple. Plays very quickly with each explorer deciding whether they should stay in the temple (and suffer or benefit from another draw card), or, return to their camp with the 'goodies' already amassed. Stay too long and you could lose everything, run too soon and you could miss further treasures. Game of fun, of nerve, bluff and double bluff with lots of cat-calling as those less fearless (some would argue - wise) souls run from the Temple's darkest depths... run-rabbit-run!!

RATING: 6.3
Simple but good press-your-luck game with a good theme. Fast-paced. Always loved by casual gamers. I love adventure themes, very particularly Indiana Jones style. It makes me love this game, and also because the simultaneous action selection mechanic.
But after multiple plays, players will eventually realize that values are faked. The game may suffer where most players would simply perform luck chasing til the end of game. Fun factor diminishes this way. I believe IMHO a meta-game penalty for the losers, or the relation with real life values (say... a cent) would remedy the situation and boost the fun factor to climax.

RATING: 8
Rating after several plays with mainly nongamers. Best with many players: There should be at least four. Easy to explain and quick to play (about 20 minutes) with above average components. The game has a serious addictive quality, and I indeed recommend to play at least twice in a row (especially if people are new to the game). Fun to play when the mood is right and there are enough players. Personally, I like it better than Piranha Pedro (which has a similar feel to it).
UPDATE: After all these years, it's still the best press your luck filler game I own. The turns and game have just the right length. I'm happy to suggest this game in any family setting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Own Incan Gold, but Diamant is really a much better version of the game. The components in Diamant are just downright superior. Having played Diamant, I like using a hidden Indy-Jones meeple in the palm to indicate your hidden choice instead of playing a card. Faster and cleaner. The crates are an upgrade from the tent cards which are just ugly in Incan Gold

The only quibble I have is the artifact cards in Incan Gold. I actually like having the artifact cards since they allow people from the backend to catch up. After someone flees, it is usually a suicide mission to stay on for the remainder of the folks. With artifacts, it makes for a more interesting game.

RATING: 6
02/2011:7
Basically playing chicken....who gets to pull out first and who tries to maintain the lead. The idea comes from risk-taking and the optimum time to call for a strategic pull out before things get too tough or dangerous.

Not a bad game, plays well with 7-8 since it is simultaneous action. Not many other games can fulfill that criteria

Own Incan Gold, but Diamant is really a much better version of the game. The components in Diamant are just downright superior. Having played Diamant, I like using a hidden Indy-Jones meeple in the palm to indicate your hidden choice instead of playing a card. Faster and cleaner. The crates are an upgrade from the tent cards which are just ugly in Incan Gold

The only quibble I have is the artifact cards in Incan Gold. I actually like having the artifact cards since they allow people from the backend to catch up. After someone flees, it is usually a suicide mission to stay on for the remainder of the folks. With artifacts, it makes for a more interesting game.

RATING: 3
Had high hopes for this - another game that is, IME, over rated.  It's push your luck which I like playing, but that itch is scratched better with other games.  

Comparisons to other such games like Can't Stop are not accurate.  In that game your odds are always visible.  Incan Gold is close to a total crap shoot.  The only basis for knowing if the odds are in your favor are by seeing how far you are into the deck and how many bad cards have popped up so far.  Simply do not understand the love for this game.

RATING: 6
Explore in a perilous mine shaft to find treasure. A very light push-your-luck game that can handle large numbers (max 8, wouldn't play with less than 6). Good for when a no-brain game is called for - closing out a game night, party gaming, playing with non-gamers. Plays extremely fast. RATING: N/A
Incan Gold; Alan R. Moon & Bruno Faidutti; quick, fun game of push-your-luck where players venture down mine shafts by turning up cards from a deck, sharing the gems they find on the way down, but before the next card is turned up, you have the chance to leave the mine and stash your finds, including any gems you get on the way out; Category: Adventure, Bluffing;  Mechanics: Simultaneous Action Selection;  Other Names: Diamond, Incan Gold, Diamantes 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Can't Stop with cards?  Not really.  You're not really playing the odds as much with this game as you are with its pappy.  Still, this is a push-your-luck game with a neat theme, and some of the coolest bits EVAR.  It requires a lot of shuffling, though, and tends to play longer than one would expect for such a light game.  In addition, this is a sort of game that improves with more players, since the extra chaos adds a higher entertainment level to the experience.

6 plays: 3 players
3 plays: 6 players
1 play: 8 players
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The Good: The cards are easier to shuffle in this version of the game, and the artifacts add another layer of reward to this push-your-luck game.  It's less expensive to purchase Incan Gold than it is to import a copy of Diamant.

The Bad: The components are a far cry from the original edition of the game, and the game looks a bit cheap by comparison.  The game is still nicely produced, and will undoubtedly stand up to a large number of plays, but crates and little plastic gems go a long way toward making this game fun to play.  Plus, you can use the artifact rule in the original version of the game without affecting the base rules that much.

The Verdict: Get Diamant.  If you can't do that, settle for Incan Gold.

1 play: 5 players

RATING: N/A
You and your fellow adventurers travel to Peru to find a ruined Incan temple and its treasures: turquoise, obsidian and gold. There are also rumors of valuable Incan artifacts. Will you chance dangers like giant spiders, mummies and fire during your search, or will you escape back to camp and safety, carrying out your loot?
\13\\13\
Incan Gold is a quick, fun and tense game in which you and other adventurers explore an old Incan temple in search of gold and treasure. In each of the five rounds, you secretly choose if you want to continue exploring the temple in search of more treasure or retreat to the safety of your camp with your share of the treasure that has been discovered so far.
\13\\13\
Each time that an explorer braves new territory, more treasure or a danger appears. When a second type of the same danger is turned over, all exposed treasure is buried, leaving the remaining adventurers with nothing. Do you flee the dangerous temple with your portion of the treasure that has been uncovered so far or do you venture into the exciting temple in search of more hidden valuables?
\13\\13\
After five rounds of exploration, whoever has the most treasure is the ultimate explorer and winner!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is a perfect nightcap game, when everyone is mentally burnt out from a long day of gaming (or drinking, for that matter). The rules are extremely easy to teach, with the players each making a single decision each turn, should I press on with the group or bail out? To complicate the decision, there is usually a fairly large pile of gems to be had for anyone tempted into leaving the group. This leads to some great table talk and plenty of cheers and groans as the group pushes their luck a hair too far or when someone sneaks away with the treasures after talking the group into opening just one more door.

There really isn't much to the game itself, but the fun it can generate with a lively group more than makes up for anything the game might lack in strategy. It almost always ends in laughter...and I can't think of any better praise than that.

RATING: 7
Group push-your-luck family/filler card game. Indiana Jones theme.  Each round, go further in the temple and risk death or escape with the gems you have. Last explorer remaining can score big (but usually is never seen again). Reimplements Diamant which uses tiles and doesn't have artifacts. I prefer cards but the tiles add a nice feel and more to the thematic build up...  This game plays well 8 players which is the main reason I have it. But it is brainless. I feel like it could use some manipulation or take-that cards but I'm sure that would ruin the pure luck and odds of it.  But this is a small issue. This is a popular filler with our friends and family that is easily enjoyed with the kids joining in. I always stay in the temple too long. When will I learn?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I can see this getting a lot of play as a nice, light filler that scales out well to 5-8 players -- a range for which I can't think of a comparably light, quick game. Diamant's brand of press-your-luck risks and rewards felt a lot like Cloud 9, but with simultaneous decisions to press on or jump ship, rather than going clockwise around the table. I like how the later rounds may encourage greater risks, not only for the allure of greater scores, but through removal of some of the hazard cards, potentially extending later rounds while shortening the deck. The gems, while attractive and thematic, are pretty clunky to deal with, especially when having to divide 15 gems by 6 people, etc.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I really enjoy this game now, after having found it underwhelming and rather mediocre on my first exposure to the game. It is a light and quick playing press your luck game with a good theme. Unfortunately the production values are not up to snuff. Most of the cards feature the same back, even though they have to be separated out - ugh! Then there's the fact that all card backs are black and white, and the turn counters are cards where you are directed to put artifacts under them for no reason. Oh, and you have to bend cards in order to use them as tents to hide your treasures.

Okay... Well, once you get over the poor components, this is a very fun party style game, and I definitely recommend it.

RATING: 4
After 2+ Plays: I don't think I like push your luck games, as I just didn't find anything interesting about this game.

--I've played the new version (Incan Gold) and it did nothing to change my opinion.

--I've since found several push-your-luck games that I like quite a bit, such as Can't Stop and Cheeky Monkey, so if you hate this don't necessarily swear of the whole genre.

RATING: 7.5
A push-your-luck game that really shines with several players. Everyone is going into a cave, and each tile either has treasure or a hazard. If two of the same hazard show up, everyone still in the cave gets nothing. You can duck out after any tile, but as people leave, the remaining players get more treasure. I absolutely love the treasure/danger buildup that occurs with several players, and it is fantastic to watch a player stock up their cache of jewels then lose it to a sudden disaster.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.25
Incan gold is a simple, entertaining filler. It's a press-your-luck mechanic where you can try and go deeper for more gems, but with a higher threat of losing everything. The gems and artifacts left behind in the tunnels complicate the decision slightly because you can leave on your own and grab all the leftovers, but it's hard to gauge when your opponents will bail for the growing leftover spoils.

The actual final scoring can be anticlimactic if one player  had a few strong outings early on, and it's tough to fall behind early because the leader can keep taking risks in order to prevent a runaway tunnel leading to a comeback, but the fun in the game is in the individual treks, not the final scoring.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
The best filler since Ricochet Robots and more fitting for people who don't want to strain their brain. Draw cards that represent a dungeon. Cards either show diamonds that are fairly distributed among those still in the dungeon, or dangers, that will cause all explorers in the dungeon to run home, losing all diamonds, if the same danger appears twice. Before each card, all players decide simultaneously if they go home (and thus securing the diamonds they have amassed so far) or continue. Also, those who go home get to snag the diamonds that have been left (those who couldn't be divided).
Absolutely wonderful game of "what the hell's the others going to do?". Most ingenous design for a simple game I've ever seen.
